<review>Friendly and pleasant staff. I'd recommend reservations, online. Indoor and outdoor seating are available, beautiful atmosphere.
They have a nice wine and cocktail selection but no blender drinks.

<userid>111336891865015635249< /userid><name>Christiane Highfill</name>< date>
1535344612522< /date>
<rating>3</rating>< Review>
First visit to this restaurant. I was with my husband and my parents.  Aesthetically, it looks nice. There was a maitre'd at the door. He was welcoming, but I didn't understand the point of the tuxedo when there weren't tablecloths on the tables. Is this supposed to be a "fine dining" establishment? There wasn't even a wine list. The room had 3 4-tops, 1 table was set up for a party of 6, and there was already a group of 9 seated, waiting for their dinner. There was also a bar-type table along the walk that seated 4.  The menu had something for everyone. The wait for our entrees was VERY long. It was a good thing we got a small plate of focaccia, 1 piece for each of us, but it took about 45 minutes before we were served. I had the short ribs. Though tender, the meat was stringy and dry. The risotto was okay. My dad ordered a burger but we had to send it back because it was undercooked.  When it came the second time, it still had a part that was undercooked, but we didn't want to bother with it anymore. My dad stated that In & Out had a better burger that what he had.  I really wanted to like this place, but I don't think I'll be returning.</Review>

This place is a joke. It doesnt even deserve a star. When I got there the 2 front hosts were flirting with clients, like if they were teenagers. <text>Spartina LA is well played balance between rustic and trendy setting nestled in the Melrose area of Los Angeles. I was in LA on a 4 hour layover coming in from a film premiere of The Hail Mary in Montana.
When an actor friend and I arrived at the peak of dinner rush, Stacia and Saran warned it might be a wait but we actually wound up being sat sooner than expected. I walked inside the courtyard to use the facilities and the interior courtyard was charming, reminiscent of a cozy seaside Mediterranean village. The deep set open view kitchen was breath-taking and the lighting were film worthy.
When I returned, we were sat and greeted by our wonderful server Tom and later by the server asst. Douglas. One of the Managers, Sophia was so sweet and kind  enough to advise us on drinks and sent us a drink on the house of which I am grateful. The pork Collar ragu was immaculately seasoned and cooked ( I could eat it all day) and the shrimp pizza rosso was great, both dishes satisfied my southern born and bred soul. Nero's fire prepared by the bartender Jahmone was excellent as was  the Regaletto sent by Sophia . The only disappointment I have is that I had to hustle out for the airport before ordering dessert.  God willing, I will return for another great time. Thank you Spartina LA!</text><Pictures>None<//Pictures><response>None<//response><gmapID>0x80c2bed30ad67e61:0xa80dcdc28fdf9de7</gmapID></record></dataset><record>

<userid>106589690397957248135</userid><user_name>Taylor Walsh</user_name><date>1598739683877< /date><Rating>5</Rating>< Review>
Really good food and very compliant with COVID pre-cautions. Sign in and sanitize at the front, wide spaced outdoor seating, and masked employees. The Burrata and Peach salad was incredible -- the right balance of salty and sweet. Bruschetta on toast was great as well as the Crab Fritters. They were a bit small for the price (3 for $16) in my opinion, but didn't lack in flavor. The menu was a little all over the place because they had items on there that had been discontinued (Little Gem Salad) and had the dinner menu out front rather than the lunch menu. Overall, good food and nice atmosphere.<//Review>

<user_name>Jonathan Guez<//user_name><date>1550249415842<//date><rating>5</rating>< Text>
Great food, highly recommended.

Came here for Valentine's Day dinner. I was disappointed to find out that it was going to be a set menu after I had made the reservation, however that changed when they gave me a link to view the selections. It was one the most robust set menu I had ever seen.

There was plenty to choose from and it ended up being 1 app, 1 pasta and 1 entre for each of us, so we got to try 6 things last night.

Unfortunately we didn't get to try the pizza since it was omitted from last night's menu, but we definitely want to go back and give that a try because we enjoyed everything else we had.

I will note that I thought the fried chicken didn't have a ton of taste, but it was good quality.

Definitely try the spaghettini with white and black garlic.< /Text>

Just another glorified-California roll joint except more expensive than most. The vast majority of their $12-$16 rolls are simply California rolls with different colored mayo squirted over it. The $7 they charge for simple salmon, tuna, etc. nigiri is too much for what this place is.

<Text>Came here for a big dinner with 8 of my girlfriends. It's located right on Melrose, with a gorgeous patio that is nicely lit. Parking is plentiful, and you can find free parking on side streets near by.

Their happy hour lasts until 7, with great options! I ordered their tequila/beet drink on HH, and it was very tasty. We also got fries, a cheese plate, and artichokes. Their beans are good as well, they give a small bowl for free.

For dinner, we all ordered a bunch of pasta. My bone marrow pasta was really delicious and flavorful and good portioned. I also tried the spaghetti which was really tasty as well. Everyone said they enjoyed their food.

Service was decent, we had to flag our waiter down a few times, but overall it was a great experience. I'd highly recommend it for a group dinner, as space is plentiful and ambiance is lovely.

Definitely will be back to try more items on the menu, but pasta seems to be the big thing here.</Text>< rate>

< text>
Oh WOW! I just came for a decent meal and a bite to eat. Was so hungry, the place at the time had 4.4 stars so my expectations were mediocre.

I was blown out of my mind from the speed food was served, and forget speed - the flavors and the way they served it.

I'd say this place is a food art factory rather than a restaurant.

All was supremely delicious and satisfying.
Had their grilled avocados for appetizer and bread which is a menu item (for good reason).

The avocados filling was a bit too lemony to my liking but the cheese countered the acidity which was a great combo.

The rye bread with Ricotta cheese and honey was a delicious crossroad of savory cheese and sweet honey.  The bread (which was grilled itself with chard marks) had touches of salt which blended magnificently with the ricotta cheese topped with honey.

The steak arrived wrapping a bunch of asparagus. Asked for medium-rare temp which was onpoint. Soft and juicy.

For dessert I had the Tiramisu which was just right balance between the the bitter, rich cacao powder and the sweet ricotta cheess and such soft but firm texture.  I had it with a double shot of espresso which had just the right level of bitterness to go with

I am amazed beyond words.<//text>

<user_id>108619561569481029670<//user_id><text>I've been to Spartina a few times and each time it blows my mind. Each dish is carefully prepared and full of flavor. The staff is very friendly and I've never had a problem with a reservation.

My boyfriend had the White Lion cocktail that has their homemade almond milk in it. I typically don't like scotch but loved the drink. We started with the chick pea farinata pancake with avocado salsa verde and everyone in our group loved it! It's unique and so flavorful. Plus it comes out at the perfect temperature to almost melt in your mouth. The wood roasted cauliflower is also delicious. They have so many delicious appetizers, salads and other dishes in case anyone doesn't want pizza or pasta.

I had the burrata cheese ravioli with spicy tomato sauce and it was delicious! We ended with the walnut pie, which I would never typically order or think I'd like but it was outstanding! Every time I come back I want to try more dishes but it's so hard because I'm already craving what I ate last time. Spartina is definitely worth it!</text>< name>

<rate>3<//rate>< review>
The food is good but not exceptional. I had the cauliflower, walnut, brown butter dish and my companion had the English pea fettucine.
Good dishes but not worth the $20 + price, especially since the ingredients are not complicated or the food that innovative. I must say though that the Mascarpone Panna Cotta dessert with Heather Honey was an excellent finish to the meal.
The restaurant  is noisy though it didn't bother me it added to the cool atmosphere and vibe of the place.
P.S I felt the owner's response on a previous bad review was arrogant and unprofessional. Restaurants at times miss their mark and I think it is the owner's responsibility to  apologize and to promise to do better, not make excuses.</review>
